# Benchmark Report (MCP): agieval_lsat - lsat_40

**Provider:** xiaomi2
**Model:** mimo-v2.5-pro

**Duration:** 114.30s


 MCP Z3 AGENT - Symbolic Reasoning

### Query
A bakery makes exactly three kinds of cookie—oatmeal, peanut butter, and sugar. Exactly three

batches of each kind of cookie are made each week (Monday through Friday) and each batch is made,
from start to finish, on a single day. The following conditions apply: No two batches of the same
kind of cookie are made on the same day. At least one batch of cookies is made on Monday. The second
batch of oatmeal cookies is made on the same day as the first batch of peanut butter cookies. The
second batch of sugar cookies is made on Thursday.Q: If no batch of cookies is made on Wednesday,
then which one of the following must be true? Answer Choices: (A)Exactly three batches of cookies
are made on Tuesday. (B)Exactly three batches of cookies are made on Friday. (C)At least two batches
of cookies are made on Monday. (D)At least two batches of cookies are made on Thursday. (E)Fewer
batches of cookies are made on Monday than on Tuesday. A: Among A through E, the answer is

  - write_and_run_z3: Write Python code using Z3 to a file and run it immediately to get results.
We capture printed stdout and stderr from running the script.

## Iteration 1



### Thinking

- Let me analyze this problem carefully.
- We have 3 kinds of cookies: oatmeal (O), peanut butter (P), sugar (S). Each kind has exactly 3 batches: O1, O2, O3, P1, P2, P3, S1, S2, S3. Days: Monday (1), Tuesday (2), Wednesday (3), Thursday (4), Friday (5).
- Constraints: 1. No two batches of the same kind are made on the same day. 2. At least one batch is made on Monday. 3. O2 is made on the same day as P1. 4. S2 is made on Thursday. 5. No batch is made on Wednesday (additional condition for the question).
- Each batch is assigned to a day (1-5, but not 3 since Wednesday is excluded).
- So effectively days are: 1 (Mon), 2 (Tue), 4 (Thu), 5 (Fri).
- For each kind, the 3 batches must be on 3 different days (from {1, 2, 4, 5}).
- Total batches: 9 batches across 4 days (Mon, Tue, Thu, Fri).
- Let me model this with Z3.
- Variables: For each batch, assign a day. - O1, O2, O3 ∈ {1, 2, 4, 5} - P1, P2, P3 ∈ {1, 2, 4, 5} - S1, S2, S3 ∈ {1, 2, 4, 5}
- Constraints: - O1, O2, O3 all different - P1, P2, P3 all different - S1, S2, S3 all different - At least one batch on Monday: Or(O1==1, O2==1, O3==1, P1==1, P2==1, P3==1, S1==1, S2==1, S3==1) - O2 == P1 - S2 == 4 - No batch on day 3 (already excluded from domain)
- Now the question asks which must be true. Let me evaluate each option:
- (A) Exactly 3 batches on Tuesday (day 2) (B) Exactly 3 batches on Friday (day 5) (C) At least 2 batches on Monday (day 1) (D) At least 2 batches on Thursday (day 4) (E) Fewer batches on Monday than on Tuesday
- For "must be true", I need to check if the negation is unsatisfiable (i.e., the option holds in all valid models).
- Let me write the Z3 code to check each option.


Looking at this problem, I need to:
1. Model 9 batches (3 per cookie type) assigned to days Mon-Fri, with Wednesday excluded
2. Encode all constraints
3. Test each answer choice to see which MUST be true (i.e., its negation is unsatisfiable)

### TOKEN USAGE - Iteration 1

  Input tokens:  6,639
  Output tokens: 1,704
  Total tokens:  8,343

### Tool Call: write_and_run_z3

  Args: {
  "filename": "cookie_batches.py",
  "code": "\nfrom z3 import *\n\n# Days: 1=Mon, 2=Tue, 3=Wed, 4=Thu, 5=Fri\n# Wednesday (3) is excluded by the problem condition\nVALID_DAYS = [1, 2, 4, 5]\n\n# Batches: O1,O2,O3 (oatmeal), P1,P2,P3 (peanut butter), S1,S2,S3 (sugar)\nO1, O2, O3 = Ints('O1 O2 O3')\nP1, P2, P3 = Ints('P1 P2 P3')\nS1, S2, S3 = Ints('S1 S2 S3')\n\nall_batches = [O1, O2, O3, P1, P2, P3, S1, S2, S3]\n\ndef base_constraints():\n    \"\"\"Return list of base constraints.\"\"\"\n    cons = []\n    # Each batch on a valid day (not Wednesday)\n    for b in all_batches:\n        cons.append(Or([b == d for d in VALID_DAYS]))\n    \n    # No two batches of same kind on same day\n    cons.append(Distinct(O1, O2, O3))\n    cons.append(Distinct(P1, P2, P3))\n    cons.append(Distinct(S1, S2, S3))\n    \n    # At least one batch on Monday\n    cons.append(Or([b == 1 for b in all_batches]))\n    \n    # O2 same day as P1\n    cons.append(O2 == P1)\n    \n    # S2 on Thursday\n    cons.append(S2 == 4)\n    \n    return cons\n\n# Count batches per day helper\ndef batches_on_day(d):\n    return Sum([If(b == d, 1, 0) for b in all_batches])\n\n# Define answer choice constraints (what each option claims)\n# (A) Exactly 3 batches on Tuesday\nopt_a = (batches_on_day(2) == 3)\n# (B) Exactly 3 batches on Friday\nopt_b = (batches_on_day(5) == 3)\n# (C) At least 2 batches on Monday\nopt_c = (batches_on_day(1) >= 2)\n# (D) At least 2 batches on Thursday\nopt_d = (batches_on_day(4) >= 2)\n# (E) Fewer batches on Monday than on Tuesday\nopt_e = (batches_on_day(1) < batches_on_day(2))\n\noptions = [(\"A\", opt_a), (\"B\", opt_b), (\"C\", opt_c), (\"D\", opt_d), (\"E\", opt_e)]\n\n# For \"must be true\", we check if the NEGATION is unsatisfiable\n# i.e., can we find a valid model where the option is FALSE?\n# If NOT (negation is unsat), then the option MUST be true.\n\nmust_be_true = []\nfor letter, constr in options:\n    s = Solver()\n    s.add(base_constraints())\n    s.add(Not(constr))  # Try to find a counterexample\n    result = s.check()\n    if result == unsat:\n        # No counterexample exists -> must be true\n        must_be_true.append(letter)\n        print(f\"Option {letter}: MUST BE TRUE (negation is unsat)\")\n    elif result == sat:\n        m = s.model()\n        print(f\"Option {letter}: NOT necessarily true (counterexample exists)\")\n        # Print the counterexample\n        day_names = {1: \"Mon\", 2: \"Tue\", 4: \"Thu\", 5: \"Fri\"}\n        for b in all_batches:\n            val = m.eval(b)\n            print(f\"  {b} = {day_names.get(int(str(val)), str(val))}\")\n        counts = {d: sum(1 for b in all_batches if m.eval(b).as_long() == d) for d in VALID_DAYS}\n        print(f\"  Day counts: {counts}\")\n    else:\n        print(f\"Option {letter}: UNKNOWN\")\n        must_be_true.append(letter + \"(unknown)\")\n\nprint()\nprint(f\"Options that must be true: {must_be_true}\")\n\n# Now use the exact required skeleton for final answer\nfound_options = []\nfor letter, constr in options:\n    s2 = Solver()\n    s2.add(base_constraints())\n    s2.add(Not(constr))\n    if s2.check() == unsat:\n        found_options.append(letter)\n\nif len(found_options) == 1:\n    print(\"STATUS: sat\")\n    print(f\"answer:{found_options[0]}\")\nelif len(found_options) > 1:\n    print(\"STATUS: unsat\")\n    print(f\"Refine: Multiple options found {found_options}\")\nelse:\n    print(\"STATUS: unsat\")\n    print(\"Refine: No options found\")\n"
}

### TOKEN USAGE - Iteration 2

  Input tokens:  8,512
  Output tokens: 2,883

### Tool Call: write_and_run_z3

  Args: {
  "filename": "cookie_enumerate.py",
  "code": "\nfrom z3 import *\n\n# Days: 1=Mon, 2=Tue, 3=Wed, 4=Thu, 5=Fri\n# Wednesday (3) is excluded\nVALID_DAYS = [1, 2, 4, 5]\n\n# Batches: O1,O2,O3 (oatmeal), P1,P2,P3 (peanut butter), S1,S2,S3 (sugar)\nO1, O2, O3 = Ints('O1 O2 O3')\nP1, P2, P3 = Ints('P1 P2 P3')\nS1, S2, S3 = Ints('S1 S2 S3')\n\nall_batches = [O1, O2, O3, P1, P2, P3, S1, S2, S3]\nbatch_names = ['O1', 'O2', 'O3', 'P1', 'P2', 'P3', 'S1', 'S2', 'S3']\n\nsolver = Solver()\n\n# Each batch on a valid day (not Wednesday)\nfor b in all_batches:\n    solver.add(Or([b == d for d in VALID_DAYS]))\n\n# No two batches of same kind on same day\nsolver.add(Distinct(O1, O2, O3))\nsolver.add(Distinct(P1, P2, P3))\nsolver.add(Distinct(S1, S2, S3))\n\n# At least one batch on Monday\nsolver.add(Or([b == 1 for b in all_batches]))\n\n# O2 same day as P1\nsolver.add(O2 == P1)\n\n# S2 on Thursday\nsolver.add(S2 == 4)\n\n# Count batches per day helper\ndef batches_on_day(d):\n    return Sum([If(b == d, 1, 0) for b in all_batches])\n\n# Enumerate all solutions\nsolutions = []\ndecision_vars = all_batches\n\nwhile solver.check() == sat:\n    m = solver.model()\n    sol = {}\n    day_names = {1: \"Mon\", 2: \"Tue\", 4: \"Thu\", 5: \"Fri\"}\n    for i, b in enumerate(all_batches):\n        sol[batch_names[i]] = day_names[int(str(m.eval(b)))]\n    \n    # Compute day counts\n    counts = {}\n    for d in VALID_DAYS:\n        counts[day_names[d]] = sum(1 for b in all_batches if int(str(m.eval(b))) == d)\n    sol['counts'] = counts\n    solutions.append(sol)\n    \n    # Block this solution\n    solver.add(Or([b != m.eval(b) for b in all_batches]))\n\nprint(f\"Total solutions: {len(solutions)}\")\nprint()\n\n# Check what's common across all solutions\n# Option A: Exactly 3 batches on Tuesday\na_true = all(s['counts']['Tue'] == 3 for s in solutions)\nprint(f\"A (exactly 3 on Tue): {a_true}\")\n\n# Option B: Exactly 3 batches on Friday\nb_true = all(s['counts']['Fri'] == 3 for s in solutions)\nprint(f\"B (exactly 3 on Fri): {b_true}\")\n\n# Option C: At least 2 batches on Monday\nc_true = all(s['counts']['Mon'] >= 2 for s in solutions)\nprint(f\"C (at least 2 on Mon): {c_true}\")\n\n# Option D: At least 2 batches on Thursday\nd_true = all(s['counts']['Thu'] >= 2 for s in solutions)\nprint(f\"D (at least 2 on Thu): {d_true}\")\n\n# Option E: Fewer on Mon than Tue\ne_true = all(s['counts']['Mon'] < s['counts']['Tue'] for s in solutions)\nprint(f\"E (Mon < Tue): {e_true}\")\n\nprint()\nprint(\"Day count distributions across all solutions:\")\nfor i, s in enumerate(solutions):\n    print(f\"  Sol {i+1}: {s['counts']} | {s}\")\n"
}

### Thinking

- Looking at the 840 solutions, none of the options A-E are universally true across all solutions. Let me look more carefully at the data.

- "No two batches of the same kind of cookie are made on the same day" - so each kind uses 3 different days out of 5.
- "each batch is made, from start to finish, on a single day" - each batch is on one day.
- "At least one batch of cookies is made on Monday."
- "The second batch of oatmeal cookies is made on the same day as the first batch of peanut butter cookies."
- "The second batch of sugar cookies is made on Thursday."
- "If no batch of cookies is made on Wednesday" - so Wednesday is excluded.
- Now looking at the solutions, none of A-E holds universally. But wait - the problem says "must be true". Let me re-examine.

- Hmm, none of them must be true. But the problem guarantees one must be true. Let me re-read the problem statement more carefully.
- "A bakery makes exactly three kinds of cookie—oatmeal, peanut butter, and sugar. Exactly three batches of each kind of cookie are made each week (Monday through Friday) and each batch is made, from start to finish, on a single day."
- Wait - "each week (Monday through Friday)" - does this mean the week is Monday through Friday? Yes.
- "The following conditions apply: No two batches of the same kind of cookie are made on the same day."
- OK so for each kind, the 3 batches are on 3 different days.
- "At least one batch of cookies is made on Monday."
- "The second batch of oatmeal cookies is made on the same day as the first batch of peanut butter cookies."
- "The second batch of sugar cookies is made on Thursday."
- "Q: If no batch of cookies is made on Wednesday, then which one of the following must be true?"
- Hmm, I'm getting 840 solutions and none of the options is universally true. Let me re-check my constraints.
- Wait - I think the issue might be that I'm not correctly interpreting "the second batch" and "the first batch". In LSAT problems, "the first batch" typically means the batch numbered 1 (i.e., O1, P1, S1 are the first batches of each kind), and "the second batch" means O2, P2, S2. The numbering is given - it's not about which day comes first.
- But actually, in many LSAT problems, "the first batch" means the one made earliest in the week, and "the second batch" means the one made second earliest. Let me reconsider.
- If "the first batch of oatmeal" means the oatmeal batch made on the earliest day, and "the second batch" means the one made on the second earliest day, then: - O1 < O2 < O3 (O1 is earliest, O3 is latest) - P1 < P2 < P3 - S1 < S2 < S3
- This is a different interpretation! Let me add these ordering constraints.
- With this interpretation: - O2 == P1 (second oatmeal same day as first peanut butter) - S2 == 4 (second sugar on Thursday)
- And O1 < O2 < O3, P1 < P2 < P3, S1 < S2 < S3.
- Let me redo the enumeration with these ordering constraints.


I see 840 solutions but none of the options holds universally. The issue is likely my interpretation of "first batch" and "second batch" - in LSAT problems, these typically refer to chronological order (earliest/latest in the week), not pre-labeled batches. Let me re-model with ordering constraints.

oatmeal batch\nO1, O2, O3 = Ints('O1 O2 O3')\nP1, P2, P3 = Ints('P1 P2 P3')\nS1, S2, S3 = Ints('S1 S2 S3')\n\nall_batches = [O1, O2, O3, P1, P2, P3, S1, S2, S3]\n\nsolver = Solver()\n\n# Each batch on a valid day (not Wednesday)\nfor b in all_batches:\n    solver.add(Or([b == d for d in VALID_DAYS]))\n\n# Chronological ordering within each kind\nsolver.add(O1 < O2, O2 < O3)\nsolver.add(P1 < P2, P2 < P3)\nsolver.add(S1 < S2, S2 < S3)\n\n# At least one batch on Monday\nsolver.add(Or([b == 1 for b in all_batches]))\n\n# Second oatmeal same day as first peanut butter\nsolver.add(O2 == P1)\n\n# sum(1 for b in all_batches if int(str(m.eval(b))) == d)\n    sol['counts'] = counts\n    solutions.append(sol)\n    \n    solver.add(Or([b != m.eval(b) for b in all_batches]))\n\nprint(f\"Total
